cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_134532_zai-claude_glm-5.2_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
# Build a debug .so that writes the threshold to out_vals[0] of each row
mkdir -p dbg
python3 -c "
import re
src=re.search(r'_CUDA_SRC = r\"\"\"(.+?)\"\"\"', open('solution.py').read(), re.S).group(1)
# after threshold loop, before gather: write threshold to out_vals[row*K+1] (debug)
src=src.replace('    // --- gather elements with M > threshold',
'    if (tid==0) out_vals[(size_t)row*K] = __int_as_float(threshold);\n    // --- gather elements with M > threshold')
open('dbg/dbg.cu','w').write(src)
"
nvcc -O3 --use_fast_math -std=c++17 -arch=sm_86 -Xcompiler=-fPIC -ccbin /usr/bin/g++-14 --shared dbg/dbg.cu -o dbg/dbg.so 2>&1 | tail -2
cat > dbg.py << 'EOF'
import torch, ctypes
lib=ctypes.CDLL('./dbg/dbg.so')
for k in [8,16,32,64]:
    for fn in ['launch_radix_'+str(k)]:
        lib.__getattribute__(fn).restype=None
    torch.manual_seed(42); b,n=2,4096
    x=torch.randn(b,n,device='cuda'); ov=torch.empty(b,k,device='cuda'); oi=torch.empty(b,k,dtype=torch.int64,device='cuda')
    lib.__getattribute__('launch_radix_'+str(k))(ctypes.c_void_p(x.data_ptr()),ctypes.c_void_p(ov.data_ptr()),ctypes.c_void_p(oi.data_ptr()),b,n,k)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    thr_raw=ov[0,0].item()
    import struct
    thr_u=struct.unpack('I',struct.pack('f',thr_raw))[0]
    # k-th largest value of row 0:
    rv=torch.topk(x[0],k,sorted=True)[0]
    print(f"k={k}: thr_uint=0x{thr_u:08x}  kth_largest_ref={rv[k-1].item():.4f} (={rv[k-1].item()})  max_ref={rv[0].item():.4f}")
EOF
uv run python dbg.py 2>&1 | grep -vE "warning:|VIRTUAL_ENV"

command (2264 chars)
cd /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260618_134532_zai-claude_glm-5.2_05_topk_bitonic/repo/problems/05_topk_bitonic
cat > thr.cu << 'EOF'
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
__device__ __forceinline__ unsigned f2u(float f){
    unsigned u=__float_as_int(f);
    if((u&0x7f800000u)==0x7f800000u && (u&0x007fffffu)) return 0;
    return (u&0x80000000u)?~u:(u|0x80000000u);
}
template<int BLOCK>
__device__ int bsum(int v,int tid){
    for(int d=16;d>0;d>>=1) v+=__shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffffu,v,d);
    __shared__ int ws[BLOCK/32]; int lane=tid&31,wid=tid>>5;
    if(lane==0) ws[wid]=v; __syncthreads();
    if(wid==0){ int x=(lane<BLOCK/32)?ws[lane]:0; for(int d=(BLOCK/32)/2;d>0;d>>=1) x+=__shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffffu,x,d); if(lane==0)ws[0]=x;} __syncthreads(); return ws[0];
}
template<int BLOCK>
__global__ void kth(const float* x, float* out, int n, int k){
    int row=blockIdx.x; const float* xr=x+(size_t)row*n; int tid=threadIdx.x;
    __shared__ unsigned st; unsigned thr=0;
    for(int bit=31;bit>=0;bit--){ unsigned cand=thr|(1u<<bit); int loc=0;
        for(int p=tid;p<n;p+=BLOCK) loc += (f2u(xr[p])>=cand);
        int tot=bsum<BLOCK>(loc,tid);
        if(tid==0) st=(tot>=k)?cand:thr; __syncthreads(); thr=st; }
    if(tid==0){ // thr = u of k-th largest. invert f2u.
        unsigned u=thr; float f;
        unsigned r = (u&0x80000000u)?(u&0x7fffffffu):~u;
        f=__int_as_float(r); out[row]=f; }
}
extern "C" void launch_kth(const float* x,float* o,int b,int n,int k){ kth<1024><<<b,1024>>>(x,o,n,k); }
EOF
nvcc -O3 --use_fast_math -std=c++17 -arch=sm_86 -Xcompiler=-fPIC -ccbin /usr/bin/g++-14 --shared thr.cu -o thr.so 2>&1 | tail -3

import torch, ctypes
lib=ctypes.CDLL('./thr.so'); lib.launch_kth.restype=None
for k in [8,16,32,64]:
    torch.manual_seed(42); b,n=2,4096
    x=torch.randn(b,n,device='cuda'); o=torch.empty(b,device='cuda')
    lib.launch_kth(ctypes.c_void_p(x.data_ptr()),ctypes.c_void_p(o.data_ptr()),b,n,k)
    torch.cuda.synchronize()
    # reference k-th largest
    ref=torch.topk(x[0],k,sorted=True)[0][k-1].item()
    print(f"k={k}: radix_kth={o[0].item():.5f}  ref_kth={ref:.5f}  match={abs(o[0].item()-ref)<1e-4}")
EOF

#include <cuda_runtime.h>
__device__ __forceinline__ unsigned f2u(float f){
    unsigned u=__float_as_int(f);
    if((u&0x7f800000u)==0x7f800000u && (u&0x007fffffu)) return 0;
    return (u&0x80000000u)?~u:(u|0x80000000u);
}
template<int BLOCK>
__device__ int bsum(int v,int tid){
    for(int d=16;d>0;d>>=1) v+=__shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffffu,v,d);
    __shared__ int ws[BLOCK/32]; int lane=tid&31,wid=tid>>5;
    if(lane==0) ws[wid]=v; __syncthreads();
    if(wid==0){ int x=(lane<BLOCK/32)?ws[lane]:0; for(int d=(BLOCK/32)/2;d>0;d>>=1) x+=__shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffffu,x,d); if(lane==0)ws[0]=x;} __syncthreads(); return ws[0];
}
template<int BLOCK,int K>
__global__ void gth(const float* x, float* ov, long long* oi, int n, int k){
    int row=blockIdx.x; const float* xr=x+(size_t)row*n; int tid=threadIdx.x;
    __shared__ unsigned st; unsigned thr=0;
    for(int bit=31;bit>=0;bit--){ unsigned cand=thr|(1u<<bit); int loc=0;
        for(int p=tid;p<n;p+=BLOCK) loc += (f2u(xr[p])>=cand);
        int tot=bsum<BLOCK>(loc,tid);
        if(tid==0) st=(tot>=k)?cand:thr; __syncthreads(); thr=st; }
    __shared__ float gsv[K]; __shared__ int gsi[K]; __shared__ int wpos;
    if(tid==0) wpos=0; __syncthreads();
    for(int p=tid;p<n;p+=BLOCK){ unsigned u=f2u(xr[p]);
        if(u>thr){int pos=atomicAdd(&wpos,1); if(pos<k){gsv[pos]=xr[p];gsi[pos]=p;}}}
    __syncthreads();
    if(wpos<k){ for(int p=tid;p<n;p+=BLOCK){ unsigned u=f2u(xr[p]);
        if(u==thr){int pos=atomicAdd(&wpos,1); if(pos<k){gsv[pos]=xr[p];gsi[pos]=p;}}} __syncthreads(); }
    for(int i=tid;i<k;i+=BLOCK){ ov[row*k+i]=gsv[i]; oi[row*k+i]=gsi[i]; }
}
extern "C" void launch_gth(const float* x,float* ov,long long* oi,int b,int n,int k){
    if(k==8) gth<1024,8><<<b,1024>>>(x,ov,oi,n,k);
    else if(k==16) gth<1024,16><<<b,1024>>>(x,ov,oi,n,k);
    else if(k==32) gth<1024,32><<<b,1024>>>(x,ov,oi,n,k);
    else gth<1024,64><<<b,1024>>>(x,ov,oi,n,k);
}
EOF

cat > thr.cu << 'EOF'
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
__device__ __forceinline__ unsigned f2u(float f){unsigned u=__float_as_int(f); if((u&0x7f800000u)==0x7f800000u&&(u&0x007fffffu))return 0; return (u&0x80000000u)?~u:(u|0x80000000u);}
template<int B>__device__ int bs(int v,int t){for(int d=16;d>0;d>>=1)v+=__shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffffu,v,d);__shared__ int w[B/32];int l=t&31,wd=t>>5;if(l==0)w[wd]=v;__syncthreads();if(wd==0){int x=(l<B/32)?w[l]:0;for(int d=(B/32)/2;d>0;d>>=1)x+=__shfl_xor_sync(0xffffffffu,x,d);if(l==0)w[0]=x;}__syncthreads();return w[0];}
template<int B>__global__ void kth(const float* x,float* o,int n,int k){int r=blockIdx.x;const float*xr=x+(size_t)r*n;int t=threadIdx.x;__shared__ unsigned st;unsigned th=0;for(int b=31;b>=0;b--){unsigned c=th|(1u<<b);int loc=0;for(int p=t;p<n;p+=B)loc+=(f2u(xr[p])>=c);int tot=bs<B>(loc,t);if(t==0)st=(tot>=k)?c:th;__syncthreads();th=st;}if(t==0)o[r]=__int_as_float(th);}
extern "C" void lk(const float*x,float*o,int b,int n,int k){kth<1024><<<b,1024>>>(x,o,n,k);}
EOF
nvcc -O3 --use_fast_math -std=c++17 -arch=sm_86 -Xcompiler=-fPIC -ccbin /usr/bin/g++-14 --shared thr.cu -o thr.so 2>&1|tail -1
cat > tm.py << 'EOF'
import torch,ctypes,statistics
lib=ctypes.CDLL('./thr.so');lib.lk.restype=None
def t(fn,it=200):
    for _ in range(30):fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize();a=[]
    for _ in range(it):
        s,e=torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True),torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True);s.record();fn();e.record();torch.cuda.synchronize();a.append(s.elapsed_time(e))
    return statistics.median(a)*1000
for (b,n,k) in [(1,131072,64),(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16)]:
    x=torch.randn(b,n,device='cuda');o=torch.empty(b,device='cuda')
    print(f"b={b} n={n} k={k}: counting_only={t(lambda:lib.lk(ctypes.c_void_p(x.data_ptr()),ctypes.c_void_p(o.data_ptr()),b,n,k)):.1f}us")
EOF

lib=solution._lib()
def t(fn,it=200):
    for _ in range(30):fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize();a=[]
    for _ in range(it):
        s,e=torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True),torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True);s.record();fn();e.record();torch.cuda.synchronize();a.append(s.elapsed_time(e))

import torch,ctypes,statistics,solution
lib=solution._lib()
def t(fn,it=200):
    for _ in range(30):fn()
    torch.cuda.synchronize();a=[]
    for _ in range(it):
        s,e=torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True),torch.cuda.Event(enable_timing=True);s.record();fn();e.record();torch.cuda.synchronize();a.append(s.elapsed_time(e))
    return statistics.median(a)*1000
b,n,k=1,131072,64
x=torch.randn(b,n,device='cuda');ov=torch.empty(b,k,device='cuda');oi=torch.empty(b,k,dtype=torch.int64,device='cuda')
xp=ctypes.c_void_p(x.data_ptr());ovp=ctypes.c_void_p(ov.data_ptr());oip=ctypes.c_void_p(oi.data_ptr())
for ss in [256,512,1024,2048,4096,8192]:
    ns=(n+ss-1)//ss
    tv=torch.empty(b,ns,k,device='cuda');ti=torch.empty(b,ns,k,dtype=torch.int32,device='cuda')
    tvp=ctypes.c_void_p(tv.data_ptr());tip=ctypes.c_void_p(ti.data_ptr())
    try:
        us=t(lambda: lib.launch_radix_big_64(xp,ovp,oip,tvp,tip,b,n,ns,ss,k))
        print(f"seg={ss} nseg={ns}: {us:.1f}us")
    except Exception as ex: print(f"seg={ss}: ERR {ex}")

-"""Single-pass top-k for RTX 3090 (SM86).
-
-The reference uses a multi-pass radix select (one pass per radix digit, ~8
-passes for fp32). For these shapes the input is small enough that pass /
-launch overhead dominates, so a SINGLE-pass kernel that reads the row once and
-selects top-k in one launch beats it comfortably.
-
-Design:
-  - block-per-row (one block reduces a whole row to top-k).
-  - each thread streams its strided slice, keeping a per-thread sorted-descending
-    register buffer of size K (K largest seen; tv[K-1] = smallest = threshold).
-  - block-merge: dump BLOCK buffers of K into shared mem, then a log2(BLOCK)-deep
-    merge-tree (merge pairs of sorted buffers keeping top-K) -> block top-K,
-    already sorted descending. O(log BLOCK) barriers, no full sort, no bank
-    conflicts from strided bitonic access.
-  - for the single very-large row (n=131072, batch=1) one block cannot saturate
-    DRAM, so a segmented two-launch path: G blocks each reduce a contiguous
-    segment to top-K into a temp buffer, then one block merge-trees G*K.
-
-Correctness: per-thread buffer size == K guarantees the global top-K survives
-to the candidate pool (any single thread sees at most K of the global top-K,
-since only K elements are >= the global k-th value), and the merge-tree
-extracts exactly the top-K sorted descending.
-
-Build: the CUDA is compiled to a standalone .so (extern "C" interface, called
-via ctypes) so it never pulls in the ML framework's C++ headers (the installed
-framework's List_inl.h is ill-formed under gcc>=14 and would fail the build).
+"""Top-k for RTX 3090 (SM86), shape-adaptive.
+
+The reference uses a multi-pass radix select (~8 passes for fp32). These shapes
+are tiny (each row is 16 KB - 512 KB), so per-call time is dominated by kernel
+work, not DRAM. Two kernels cover the deck, picked per (k, n):
+
+  * Small k (1, 8, 16) -- per-row register cascade. One block per row; each
+    thread streams a strided slice keeping a sorted-descending register buffer
+    of size K (the K largest it has seen). Buffers are merged across the block
+    by a log2(BLOCK)-deep merge-tree in shared mem (stride K+1 to dodge 32-way
+    bank conflicts). All-register, static-index cascade (a dynamic index into a
+    register array spills to local memory; a shared-mem min-heap was tried and
+    is slower due to shmem load latency in the dependent sift-down).
+
+  * Large k (32, 64) -- per-row radix-256 histogram select. Four byte-passes
+    (MSB first) build the monotonic uint of the k-th largest via a 256-bin
+    histogram, then gather + in-shmem bitonic sort. ~12 barriers total vs ~96
+    for a 1-bit radix, and 4x fewer row reads -- far cheaper than the O(n*K)
+    cascade once K is large.
+
+  * The single very-large row (n=131072, k=64) -- segmented radix: many blocks
+    each radix-select their contiguous segment to top-K into a temp buffer,
+    then one block radix-selects the merged candidates. Keeps the whole GPU
+    busy instead of one block.
+
+Correctness: the per-thread cascade buffer is size K (any single thread sees
+at most K of the global top-K, since only K elements are >= the k-th value), so
+the global top-K survives to the merge. Radix finds the exact k-th largest's
+monotonic uint (the largest value with count(>=v) >= k), so the gather collects
+exactly the top-K (ties filled to K). Both paths return values sorted
+descending; indices are checked leniently by the harness (gather-vs-reference).
+
+Build: the CUDA is compiled to a standalone .so (extern "C", called via ctypes)
+so it never pulls in the ML framework's C++ headers -- the installed framework's
+List_inl.h is ill-formed under gcc>=14 and would fail an extension build.
 """

import torch, solution
# edge cases per shape
tests = [
    ("all zeros", lambda: torch.zeros(8, 4096, device='cuda')),
    ("all equal 3.5", lambda: torch.full((8,4096),3.5,device='cuda')),
    ("binary 0/1", lambda: (torch.rand(8,4096,device='cuda')>0.5).float()),
    ("with neg", lambda: torch.randn(8,4096,device='cuda')*100-50),
    ("few unique", lambda: torch.randint(0,5,(8,4096),device='cuda').float()),
]
ok=True
for (b,n,k) in [(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(1,131072,64),(128,4096,1)]:
    for name, gen in tests:
        torch.manual_seed(7); x=gen()
        if x.shape!=(b,n): 
            xb=torch.empty(b,n,device='cuda'); xb[:,:x.shape[1] if x.shape[1]<=n else n]=x[:,:n] if x.shape[1]>=n else x
            x=xb
        m=solution.Model(b,n,k).cuda().eval()
        v,idx=m(x); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        rv,ri=torch.topk(x,k,sorted=True)
        vm=torch.allclose(v,rv,atol=1e-4)
        gm=torch.allclose(torch.gather(x,1,idx.long().clamp(0,n-1)),rv,atol=1e-4)
        if not(vm and gm):
            ok=False; print(f"FAIL {name} b={b} n={n} k={k}: vals={vm} gather={gm}")
print("ALL OK" if ok else "SOME FAILED")
EOF

import torch, solution
def gen(kind,b,n):
    if kind=="zeros": return torch.zeros(b,n,device='cuda')
    if kind=="const": return torch.full((b,n),3.5,device='cuda')
    if kind=="binary": return (torch.rand(b,n,device='cuda')>0.5).float()
    if kind=="few": return torch.randint(0,5,(b,n),device='cuda').float()
    return torch.randn(b,n,device='cuda')*100-50  # gauss neg
ok=True
for (b,n,k) in [(64,8192,8),(32,16384,32),(16,12000,16),(1,131072,64),(128,4096,1)]:
    for kind in ["zeros","const","binary","few","gauss"]:
        torch.manual_seed(7); x=gen(kind,b,n)
        m=solution.Model(b,n,k).cuda().eval()
        v,idx=m(x); torch.cuda.synchronize()
        rv,ri=torch.topk(x,k,sorted=True)
        vm=torch.allclose(v,rv,atol=1e-4)
        gm=torch.allclose(torch.gather(x,1,idx.long().clamp(0,n-1)),rv,atol=1e-4)
        inrange = (idx.long().min()>=0) and (idx.long().max()<n)
        if not(vm and gm and inrange):
            ok=False; print(f"FAIL {kind} b={b} n={n} k={k}: vals={vm} gather={gm} inrange={inrange}")
print("ALL OK" if ok else "SOME FAILED")
EOF

+---
+name: kbhard-topk-3090
+description: KBHard 05_topk_bitonic on 3090 — achieved 0.05 geomean (2.15x torch.topk); shape-adaptive cascade+radix design
+metadata:
+  type: reference
+---
+
+05_topk_bitonic scored on RTX 3090 (936 GB/s DRAM). Achieved geomean
+peak_fraction ~0.05 (RESULT: LOW vs the 0.1 generic threshold, but that
+threshold is unreachable for top-k on 3090 — it is launch-overhead-bound:
+every row is 16KB-512KB, so even a zero-work kernel bottoms out at ~11us
+dispatch floor). torch.topk itself scores ~0.023 geomean; 0.05 is ~2.15x it.
+
+Per-shape (mine / torch.topk us): shape0 (1,131072,64)=54/68,
+shape1 (64,8192,8)=19/71, shape2 (32,16384,32)=40/71, shape3 (16,12000,16)=30/66,
+shape4 (128,4096,1)=14/41. Beats torch.topk on every shape.
+
+Winning design (shape-adaptive):
+- k<=16: per-row REGISTER cascade. One block/row; each thread keeps a size-K
+  sorted-desc register buffer, merged across the block by a log2(BLOCK) merge-tree
+  in shmem (stride K+1 to dodge 32-way bank conflicts). CRITICAL: dynamic
+  indexing into a register array spills to local memory (1389 .local refs,
+  ~10x slower) — use a fully-unrolled conditional-cascade with STATIC indices.
+  A shmem min-heap (O(logK)) is SLOWER than the O(K) register cascade because
+  the sift-down's dependent shmem-load chain (~30cyc/level) beats 1cyc registers.
+- k>=32: per-row radix-256 histogram select (4 byte-passes, ~12 syncs, NOT
+  1-bit radix which is ~96 syncs and sync-bound). Then in-shmem cooperative
+  bitonic sort. Sorting a LOCAL register array via pointer also spills for
+  large K — sort in shmem directly.
+- n=131072 single row: segmented radix (G blocks reduce segments, 1 merges).
+  seg_size=2048 optimal. Cooperative-grid radix would be faster but is fiddly
+  via ctypes (cudaLaunchCooperativeKernel + cudadevrt) and was not attempted.
+
+Build gotcha: torch 2.11's List_inl.h is ill-formed under gcc>=14 (needs
+typename) — avoids this by compiling a standalone .so (extern "C", nvcc
+-ccbin g++-14) called via ctypes with raw data_ptr(), never including
+torch/extension.h. See [[kbhard-run-can-land-on-3090]].

Done. Here's a summary of the work. ## Result `solution.py` passes `check.py` (all 5 shapes × 3 seeds × numeric-stress cases + edge cases) and scores **geomean peak_fraction ≈ 0.0495** — about **2.15× torch.topk** (which itself scores ~0.023). It beats torch.topk on every shape: | shape (b,n,k) | mine | torch.topk | |---|---|---| | (1, 131072, 64) | 54µs | 68µs | | (64, 8192, 8) | 19µs | 71µs | | (32, 16384, 32) | 40µs | 71µs | | (16, 12000, 16) | 30µs | 66µs | | (128, 4096, 1) | 14µs | 41µs | Forbidden-op scan clean, ruff clean, framework = `cuda_raw`. ## Design (shape-adaptive) The problem is launch-overhead-bound (rows are 16KB–512KB; the dispatch floor is ~11µs), so the win is minimizing per-call kernel work, not saturating DRAM. Three kernels, picked per (k, n): - **k ≤ 16** — per-row **register cascade**: one block/row, each thread keeps a size-K sorted-descending register buffer, merged across the block by a log₂(BLOCK) merge-tree in shared memory (stride K+1 to dodge 32-way bank conflicts). - **k ≥ 32** — per-row **radix-256 histogram select**: 4 byte-passes (~12 barriers, not ~96 like 1-bit radix which is sync-bound), then in-shmem bitonic sort. - **n = 131072** — **segmented radix**: G blocks each radix-select their segment, one block merges. ## Hard-won gotchas (the real work) 1. **Register spill kills it**: dynamic indexing `tv[q]` into a register array spills to local memory (1389 `.local` refs → 10× slower). Fixed with a fully-unrolled conditional-cascade using static indices only. A shmem min-heap (O(log K)) was *slower* than the O(K) register cascade due to dependent shmem-load latency. 2. **gcc-15/16 can't build torch extensions** — torch 2.11's `List_inl.h` is ill-formed (missing `typename`). Worked around by compiling a standalone `.so` with `extern "C"` + `nvcc -ccbin g++-14`, called via ctypes with raw `data_ptr()` — never includes `torch/extension.h`. 3. **Bank conflicts** in the merge-tree (stride-K buffers, K=32 → 32-way conflict) fixed with K+1 stride. 4. **Load-latency hiding** via tiled prefetch in the streaming loop. The biggest remaining drag is shape 0 (single 131072-row, k=64) at ~0.012 — fundamentally hard without a cooperative-grid radix (fiddly via ctypes, not attempted). That caps geomean around ~0.07–0.09 even with all other shapes at the dispatch floor.
